### Temperature: 0.0 | Problem 78 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A newspaper costs $4 on Sunday and $1 the rest of the days of the week. If a hotel orders twice as many papers on Sunday as it does the rest of the days of the week and pays $210 per week for newspapers, how many newspapers does it buy on Monday?
Choices:
  A: 15
  B: 30
  C: 45
  D: 60
  E: 75
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's call the number of newspapers the hotel orders on Sunday "x".
  The hotel orders twice as many newspapers on Sunday as it does the rest of the days of the week, so it orders "2y" newspapers on the other days.
  The cost of x newspapers on Sunday is 4x dollars.
  The cost of 2y newspapers on the other days is 2y dollars.
  The total cost of newspapers per week is 210 dollars.
  We can write an equation: 4x + 6y = 210 (since there are 7 days in a week and the hotel orders twice as many newspapers on Sunday as it does on each of the other 6 days).
  We need to find y, the number of newspapers the hotel orders on Monday.
  We can solve for y and then multiply by 2 to find x, the number of newspapers the hotel orders on Sunday.
  First, we can simplify the equation: 2x + 3y = 105.
  We know that x = 2y, so we can substitute: 2(2y) + 3y = 105.
  Solving for y: 7y = 105, y = 15.
  Therefore, the hotel orders 15 newspapers on Monday.
  The answer is A: 15.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  Let's call the number of newspapers the hotel orders on Sunday "x".
  The hotel orders twice as many newspapers on Sunday as it does the rest of the days of the week, so it orders "2y" newspapers on the other days.
  The cost of x newspapers on Sunday is 4x dollars.
  The cost of 2y newspapers on the other days is 2y dollars.
  The total cost of newspapers per week is 210 dollars.
  We can write an equation: 4x + 6y = 210 (since there are 7 days in a week and the hotel orders twice as many newspapers on Sunday as it does on each of the other 6 days).
  We need to find y, the number of newspapers the hotel orders on Monday.
  We can solve for y and then multiply by 2 to find x, the number of newspapers the hotel orders on Sunday.
  First, we can simplify the equation: 2x + 3y = 105.
  We know that x = 2y, so we can substitute: 2(2y) + 3y = 105.
  Solving for y: 7y = 105, y = 15.
  Therefore, the hotel orders 15 newspapers on Monday.
  The answer is A: 15.
Action: Answer("A")

### Temperature: 0.0 | Problem 79 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The length of the ribbon was originally 30 cm. It was reduced in the ratio 5 : 3. What is its length now?
Choices:
  A: 18
  B: 30
  C: 6
  D: 15
  E: 12
Response 0:
Thought:
  The original length of the ribbon was 30 cm.
  The ribbon was reduced in the ratio 5:3.
  This means that the new length of the ribbon is (3/5) of the original length.
  We can find the new length by multiplying the original length by (3/5).
  New length = 30 x (3/5) = 18 cm.
  Therefore, the length of the ribbon now is 18 cm.
Action: Answer("A")

### Temperature: 0.0 | Problem 80 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Allen starts from X, goes to Y. At the same time Bob starts from Y and goes towards X. Once Allen reaches Y he changes his direction and returns to X. Once Bob reaches X, he changes his direction and returns to Y. Throughout Allen travels at 54 kmph and Bob travels at 78kmph. By the time they meet for the second time, Bob covers 48 km more than Allen. Find the distance between X and Y.
Choices:
  A: 144km
  B: 72 km
  C: 126km
  D: 84 km
  E: 48km
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume the distance between X and Y is d km.
  Let's assume the time taken by both Allen and Bob to meet for the second time is t hours.
  Let's assume the distance covered by Allen from X to Y is x km.
  Therefore, the distance covered by Bob from Y to X is (d - x) km.
  The time taken by Allen to cover x km is (x/54) hours.
  The time taken by Bob to cover (d - x) km is ((d - x)/78) hours.
  The time taken by Allen to cover the remaining (d - x) km is ((d - x)/54) hours.
  The time taken by Bob to cover the remaining x km is (x/78) hours.
  The total time taken by Allen to meet Bob for the second time is (x/54) + ((d - x)/54) hours.
  The total time taken by Bob to meet Allen for the second time is (x/78) + ((d - x)/78) hours.
  As both Allen and Bob meet for the second time, the total time taken by both of them should be equal.
  Therefore, (x/54) + ((d - x)/54) = (x/78) + ((d - x)/78)
  Solving the above equation, we get x = (d/3)
  Given that Bob covers 48 km more than Allen by the time they meet for the second time.
  Therefore, (d - x) + 48 = x
  Solving the above equation, we get x = (d - 48)/2
  Equating both the values of x, we get (d/3) = (d - 48)/2
  Solving the above equation, we get d = 144 km
  Therefore, the distance between X and Y is 144 km.
  The answer is A: 144km.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:

  Solving the above equation, we get x = (d/3)
  Given that Bob covers 48 km more than Allen by the time they meet for the second time.
  Therefore, (d - x) + 48 = x
  Solving the above equation, we get x = (d - 48)/2
  Equating both the values of x, we get (d/3) = (d - 48)/2
  Solving the above equation, we get d = 144 km
  Therefore, the distance between X and Y is 144 km.
  The answer is A: 144km.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 9:
Thought:
  Let's assume the distance between X and Y is d km.
  Let's assume the time taken by both Allen and Bob to meet for the second time is t hours.
  Let's assume the distance covered by Allen from X to Y is x km.
  Therefore, the distance covered by Bob from Y to X is (d - x) km.
  The time taken by Allen to cover x km is (x/54) hours.
  The time taken by Bob to cover (d - x) km is ((d - x)/78) hours.
  The time taken by Allen to cover the remaining (d - x) km is ((d - x)/54) hours.
  The time taken by Bob to cover the remaining x km is (x/78) hours.
  The total time taken by Allen to meet Bob for the second time is (x/54) + ((d - x)/54) hours.
  The total time taken by Bob to meet Allen for the second time is (x/78) + ((d - x)/78) hours.
  As both Allen and Bob meet for the second time, the total time taken by both of them should be equal.
  Therefore, (x/54) + ((d - x)/54) = (x/78) + ((d - x)/78)
  Solving the above equation, we get x = (d/3)
  Given that Bob covers 48 km more than Allen by the time they meet for the second time.
  Therefore, (d - x) + 48 = x
  Solving the above equation, we get x = (d - 48)/2
  Equating both the values of x, we get (d/3) = (d - 48)/2
  Solving the above equation, we get d = 144 km
  Therefore, the distance between X and Y is 144 km.
  The answer is A: 144km.

### Temperature: 0.0 | Problem 81 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A jeep travels a certain distance taking 6 hours in the forward journey. During the return journey, it increased its speed by 12km/hr and took 4 hours. What is the distance travelled by the jeep?
Choices:
  A: 126km
  B: 144km
  C: 127km
  D: 228km
  E: 128km
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume the speed of the jeep in the forward journey is x km/hr.
  Let's use the formula: Distance = Speed x Time
  Distance covered in the forward journey = x * 6
  Let's assume the speed of the jeep in the return journey is (x+12) km/hr.
  Distance covered in the return journey = (x+12) * 4
  As the distance covered in the forward journey is equal to the distance covered in the return journey, we can equate the two equations.
  x * 6 = (x+12) * 4
  Solving the above equation, we get x = 18 km/hr
  Distance covered in the forward journey = x * 6 = 18 * 6 = 108 km
  Therefore, the distance travelled by the jeep is 2 * 108 = 216 km (forward and return journey)
Action: Answer("D")

### Temperature: 0.0 | Problem 82 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The number of water lilies on a certain lake doubles every two days. If there is exactly one water lily on the lake, it takes 60 days for the lake to be fully covered with water lilies. In how many days will the lake be fully covered with lilies, if initially there were 64 water lilies on it?
Choices:
  A: 15
  B: 28
  C: 30
  D: 53
  E: 59
Response 0:
Thought:
  If the number of water lilies doubles every two days, then the number of lilies after n days is 2^(n/2).
  If there is exactly one water lily on the lake, it takes 60 days for the lake to be fully covered with water lilies.
  Therefore, 2^(60/2) = 2^30 = the number of lilies on the lake after 60 days if there was initially one lily.
  If initially there were 64 water lilies on the lake, then the number of lilies after n days is 64 * 2^(n/2).
  We want to find the number of days it takes for the lake to be fully covered with lilies, which means the number of lilies is equal to the number of lilies after 60 days.
  Therefore, 64 * 2^(n/2) = 2^30.
  Dividing both sides by 64, we get 2^(n/2) = 2^25.
  Taking the square of both sides, we get 2^n = 2^50.
  Therefore, n = 50.
  The answer is 50 days.
Action: Answer("None of the Above")

### Temperature: 0.0 | Problem 83 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A train M leaves City A at 5 am and reaches City B at 9am. Another train N leaves City B at 7am and reaches City A at 1030am. At what time do the 2 trains cross one another?
Choices:
  A: 1 hr 23 min
  B: 1 hr 15 min
  C: 1 hr 8 min
  D: 56 min
  E: 55 min
Response 0:
Thought:
  Train M travels for 4 hours (5am to 9am) before it meets Train N.
  Train N travels for 3.5 hours (7am to 10:30am) before it meets Train M.
  Let's assume that the two trains meet after x hours of Train N's journey.
  Therefore, Train M would have traveled for (x+2) hours when they meet.
  The distance traveled by both trains is equal.
  Let's assume that the speed of Train M is S1 and the speed of Train N is S2.
  Distance = Speed x Time
  Distance traveled by Train M = S1(x+2)
  Distance traveled by Train N = S2x
  Since both trains travel the same distance, we can equate the two expressions:
  S1(x+2) = S2x
  Solving for x, we get x = 4S1/(3S2-S1)
  We can substitute the values of S1 and S2 to get x.
  Once we have x, we can add it to the start time of Train N (7am) to get the time when the two trains meet.
  Therefore, we can calculate the answer.
  The answer is A: 1 hr 23 min.
Action: Answer("A")

  Once we have x, we can add it to the start time of Train N (7am) to get the time when the two trains meet.
  Therefore, we can calculate the answer.
  The answer is A: 1 hr 23 min.
Action: Answer("A")

  Distance = Speed x Time
  Distance traveled by Train M = S1(x+2)
  Distance traveled by Train N = S2x

### Temperature: 0.0 | Problem 84 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: The average (arithmetic mean) of the weight of 10 vehicles is 12.2 tons. The average weight of the group of vehicles increased by 2.6 tons after a new heavy duty truck was added to the group? What is the weight in tons of the heavy duty truck?
Choices:
  A: 40.8
  B: 41.6
  C: 42.2
  D: 43.5
  E: 44.8
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's call the weight of the new heavy duty truck "x".
  The sum of the weights of the 10 original vehicles is 10 * 12.2 = 122 tons.
  After adding the new truck, there are 11 vehicles in the group.
  The new average weight is 12.2 + 2.6 = 14.8 tons.
  The sum of the weights of all 11 vehicles is 11 * 14.8 = 162.8 tons.
  The sum of the weights of the 10 original vehicles plus the weight of the new truck is 122 + x.
  We can set up an equation: (122 + x) / 11 = 14.8
  Solving for x: 122 + x = 162.8
  x = 40.8
  Therefore, the weight of the heavy duty truck is 40.8 tons.
Action: Answer("A")

### Temperature: 0.0 | Problem 85 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: 10kg of a mixture contains 30% sand and 70% clay. In order to make the mixture contain equal quantities of clay and sand how much of the mixture is to be removed and replaced with pure sand?
Choices:
  A: 10/7
  B: 20/7
  C: 30/7
  D: 40/7
  E: 50/7
Response 0:
Thought:
- The current mixture is 30% sand and 70% clay.
- We want to make the mixture contain equal quantities of clay and sand.
- This means we want the mixture to be 50% sand and 50% clay.
- We need to remove some of the mixture and replace it with pure sand.
- Let's say we remove x kg of the mixture.
- Then we add x kg of pure sand.
- The amount of sand in the new mixture will be 0.3 * (10 - x) + x.
- The amount of clay in the new mixture will be 0.7 * (10 - x).
- We want the amount of sand and clay to be equal, so we set these two expressions equal to each other and solve for x.

Calculation:
0.3 * (10 - x) + x = 0.7 * (10 - x)
3 - 0.3x + x = 7 - 0.7x
0.4x = 4
x = 10

- We need to remove 10 kg of the mixture and replace it with 10 kg of pure sand.

Action: Answer("A")

Question: Find the total no. of distinct bike no.'s that can beformed using 2 letters followed by 2 no.'s. How many letters need to be distinct?
Choices:
  A: 74453
  B: 64543
  C: 74325
  D: 65000
  E: 97656

Thought:
  We need to find the total number of distinct bike numbers that can be formed using 2 letters followed by 2 numbers.
  There are 26 letters in the English alphabet.
  There are 10 digits (0-9).

  The order of the letters and digits matters.
  Therefore, the total number of distinct bike numbers that can be formed is 26*26*10*10 = 67600.
  The number of letters that need to be distinct is 2.

### Temperature: 0.0 | Problem 87 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: If Jill needed to buy 10 bottles of soda for a party in which 8 people attended, how many bottles of soda will she need to buy for a party in which 12 people are attending?
Choices:
  A: 6
  B: 8
  C: 10
  D: 12
  E: 14
Response 0:
Thought:
  Jill needed 10 bottles of soda for 8 people.
  So, each person drank 10/8 = 1.25 bottles of soda.
  To find out how many bottles of soda Jill needs for 12 people, we can use the ratio of bottles of soda to people.
  If 8 people need 10 bottles of soda, then 1 person needs 10/8 = 1.25 bottles of soda.
  Therefore, 12 people will need 12 * 1.25 = 15 bottles of soda.
  The answer is not one of the choices.
Action: Answer("None of the Above")

### Temperature: 0.0 | Problem 88 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: What will be the cost of gardening 1-metre – broad boundary around a rectangular plot having perimeter of 340 metres at the rate of 10 per square metre?
Choices:
  A: 3400
  B: 1700
  C: 3440
  D: Cannot be determined
  E: None of these
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume the length of the rectangular plot is L and the breadth is B.
  The perimeter of the rectangular plot is 2(L+B) = 340 meters.
  L+B = 170 meters.
  The length of the plot covered by gardening will be L+2 and the breadth will be B+2.
  The area of the gardening plot will be (L+2)(B+2) square meters.
  The cost of gardening 1 square meter is 10 dollars.
  Therefore, the cost of gardening (L+2)(B+2) square meters will be 10(L+2)(B+2) dollars.
  We need to find the value of (L+2)(B+2).
  We know that L+B = 170 meters.
  We can write L = 170 - B.
  Substituting this value of L in the expression (L+2)(B+2), we get (170-B+2)(B+2).
  Simplifying this expression, we get (B^2 + 168B + 336).
  We need to find the value of B^2 + 168B + 336.
  We can complete the square to get (B+84)^2 - 168.
  Therefore, (B^2 + 168B + 336) = (B+84)^2 - 168.
  We know that (L+2)(B+2) = (B^2 + 168B + 336).
  Therefore, (L+2)(B+2) = (B+84)^2 - 168.
  We can substitute this value in the expression 10(L+2)(B+2) to get the final answer.
  Therefore, the answer is C: 3440.
Action: Answer("C")

Topic: Math
Question: The capacity of a tank of dimensions (8 m × 6 m × 2.5 m) is
Choices:
  A: 120 litres
  B: 1200 litres
  C: 12000 litres
  D: 120000 litres
  E: None of these
Response 0:
Thought:
  The volume of the tank can be calculated by multiplying its dimensions.
  Volume = 8 m x 6 m x 2.5 m = 120 m^3
  1 m^3 = 1000 litres
  Therefore, the capacity of the tank is 120 m^3 x 1000 litres/m^3 = 120000 litres.
  The answer is D: 120000 litres.
Action: Answer("D")

### Temperature: 0.0 | Problem 90 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Calculate the percentage gain of a merchant who purchased 90 kg of oranges for Rs. 450 and sold the whole lot at the rate of Rs. 7.50 per kg.
Choices:
  A: 50 %
  B: 60 %
  C: 55 %
  D: 70 %
  E: 58%
Response 0:
Thought:
  The cost price of 1 kg of oranges is 450/90 = Rs. 5.
  The selling price of 1 kg of oranges is Rs. 7.50.
  The profit made on 1 kg of oranges is Rs. 7.50 - Rs. 5 = Rs. 2.50.
  The profit made on 90 kg of oranges is 90 x Rs. 2.50 = Rs. 225.
  The percentage gain is (Profit / Cost Price) x 100.
  The percentage gain is (225 / 450) x 100 = 50%.
  Therefore, the answer is A: 50%.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:
Thought:
  The cost price of 1 kg of oranges is 450/90 = Rs. 5.

  The percentage gain is (225 / 450) x 100 = 50%.
  Therefore, the answer is A: 50%.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 9:
Thought:
  The cost price of 1 kg of oranges is 450/90 = Rs. 5.
  The selling price of 1 kg of oranges is Rs. 7.50.
  The profit made on 1 kg of oranges is Rs. 7.50 - Rs. 5 = Rs. 2.50.
  The profit made on 90 kg of oranges is 90 x Rs. 2.50 = Rs. 225.
  The percentage gain is (Profit / Cost Price) x 100.
  The percentage gain is (225 / 450) x 100 = 50%.
  Therefore, the answer is A: 50%.
Action: Answer("A")

Topic: Math
Question: There is well of depth 30m and frog is at bottom of the well. He jumps 3m up one day and falls back 2m down the same day. How many days will it take for the frog to come out of the well?
Choices:
  A: 25 days
  B: 26 days
  C: 27 days
  D: 28 days
  E: 29 days
Response 0:
Thought:
  The frog jumps 3m up and falls back 2m down each day.
  Therefore, the frog makes a net progress of 1m each day.
  The frog needs to cover a distance of 30m to come out of the well.
  Therefore, the frog will take 30 days to come out of the well.
  However, the frog will come out on the 30th day, not after the 30th day.
  Therefore, the answer is not 30 days.
  The answer is 30 - 1 = 29 days.
Action: Answer("E")

### Temperature: 0.0 | Problem 93 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Joe's age, Joe's sister's age and Joe’s fathers age sums up to 100. When Joe is as old as his father, Joe's sister will be twice as old as now. When Joe is as old as his father then his father is twice as old as when his sister was as old as her father. Find the age of Joe's father?
Choices:
  A: 45
  B: 48
  C: 50
  D: 55
  E: 58
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume Joe's age is J, Joe's sister's age is S, and Joe's father's age is F.
  We know that J + S + F = 100.
  We also know that when Joe is as old as his father, Joe's sister will be twice as old as now.
  This means that F - J = S + (S * 2) = 3S.
  We also know that when Joe is as old as his father then his father is twice as old as when his sister was as old as her father.
  This means that F - J = 2(F - S).
  We can use these two equations to solve for S and F.
  Simplifying the first equation, we get S = (F - J) / 3.
  Substituting this into the second equation, we get F - J = 2(F - (F - J) / 3).
  Solving for J, we get J = (F - 30) / 3.
  Substituting this into the first equation, we get (F - 30) / 3 + S + F = 100.
  Simplifying this equation, we get F + S = 110.
  Substituting S = (F - J) / 3, we get F + (F - J) / 3 = 110.
  Substituting J = (F - 30) / 3, we get F + (F - (F - 30) / 3) / 3 = 110.
  Solving for F, we get F = 48.
  Therefore, the age of Joe's father is 48.
  The answer is B: 48.
Action: Answer("B")

### Temperature: 0.0 | Problem 94 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Christopher and Jonathan were having bets. They decide that a coin will be flipped twenty times and each time it turns heads, Christopher will give $2 to Jonathan and each time it turns out to be Tails, Jonathan will give 3$ to Christopher. After flipping for twenty times none of the both won or lost any amount.
How many times did the coin landed on Heads ?
Choices:
  A: 10
  B: 23
  C: 16
  D: 18
  E: 12
Response 0:
Thought:
  Christopher gives $2 to Jonathan for each Heads.
  Jonathan gives $3 to Christopher for each Tails.
  Let's assume the coin landed on Heads x times.
  Therefore, the coin landed on Tails (20 - x) times.
  Christopher gave $2x to Jonathan.
  Jonathan gave $3(20 - x) to Christopher.
  The total amount given by Christopher and Jonathan is equal to zero.
  2x - 3(20 - x) = 0
  2x - 60 + 3x = 0
  5x = 60
  x = 12
  Therefore, the coin landed on Heads 12 times.
  The answer is E: 12.
Action: Answer("E")

Action: Answer("E")
Response 7:
Thought:
  Christopher gives $2 to Jonathan for each Heads.
  Jonathan gives $3 to Christopher for each Tails.
  Let's assume the coin landed on Heads x times.
  Therefore, the coin landed on Tails (20 - x) times.
  Christopher gave $2x to Jonathan.
  Jonathan gave $3(20 - x) to Christopher.
  The total amount given by Christopher and Jonathan is equal to zero.
  2x - 3(20 - x) = 0
  2x - 60 + 3x = 0
  5x = 60
  x = 12
  Therefore, the coin landed on Heads 12 times.
  The answer is E: 12.

### Temperature: 0.0 | Problem 95 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: Kevin drove from A to B at a constant speed of 70 mph. Once he reached B, he turned right around with pause, and returned to A at a constant speed of 90 mph. Exactly 3 hours before the end of his trip, he was still approaching B, only 70 miles away from it. What is the distance between A and B?
Choices:
  A: 180
  B: 90
  C: 270
  D: 360
  E: None of the above
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's call the distance between A and B "d".
  Let's call the time it takes Kevin to travel from A to B "t".
  We know that Kevin's speed from A to B is 70 mph, so we can use the formula distance = speed x time to get d = 70t.
  We also know that Kevin's speed from B to A is 90 mph, so the time it takes him to travel from B to A is also "t".
  We know that 3 hours before the end of his trip, he was still approaching B, only 70 miles away from it.
  This means that at that point, he had already traveled a distance of d - 70 miles.
  We can use the formula distance = speed x time again to get d - 70 = 90(t - 3).
  We now have two equations with two variables, which we can solve for "d".
  Solving for "t" in the first equation, we get t = d/70.
  Substituting this into the second equation, we get d - 70 = 90((d/70) - 3).
  Simplifying this equation, we get d = 630.
  Therefore, the distance between A and B is 630 miles.
Action: Answer("E")

### Temperature: 0.0 | Problem 96 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: I know a 5 digit number having a property that with a 1 after it, it is three times as large as it would be with a 1 before it.
What is that number?
Choices:
  A: 42857
  B: 32456
  C: 76523
  D: 24567
  E: 43566
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume the 5 digit number is "abcde".
  According to the problem, if we add 1 after the number, it becomes "abcde1" and it is three times as large as it would be with a 1 before it, which is "1abcde".
  So, we can write the equation as 3(1abcde) = abcde1.
  Multiplying 3 with "1abcde" gives us 300000 + 3abcde.
  Therefore, the equation becomes 300000 + 3abcde = abcde1.
  Rearranging the equation, we get abcde = (100001/2).
  Therefore, the answer is A: 42857.
Action: Answer("A")
Response 1:

### Temperature: 0.0 | Problem 97 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: An organization decided to raise Rs. 6 lakh by collecting equal contribution from each of its employees. If each of them had contributed Rs. 60 extra, the contribution would have been Rs. 6.24 lakh. How many employees are there in that organization?
Choices:
  A: 300
  B: 200
  C: 400
  D: 100
  E: 500
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume there are 'n' employees in the organization.
  Each employee contributes 'x' amount of money.
  Therefore, the total amount collected is n*x.
  According to the problem, n*x = 6,00,000 and n*(x+60) = 6,24,000.
  We can solve these equations to find the value of 'n'.
  n*x + n*60 = 6,24,000
  n*x = 6,00,000
  Substituting the value of n*x in the first equation, we get:
  6,00,000 + n*60 = 6,24,000
  n*60 = 24,000
  n = 400
  Therefore, there are 400 employees in the organization.
  The answer is C: 400.
Action: Answer("C")

### Temperature: 0.0 | Problem 98 of 100 ###
Topic: Math
Question: A man divides Rs 8600 among 5 sons, 4 daughters and 2 nephews. If each daughter receives four times as much as each nephew, and each son receives five as much as each nephew. How much does each daughter receive ?
Choices:
  A: Rs 400
  B: Rs 500
  C: Rs 600
  D: Rs 700
  E: Rs 800
Response 0:
Thought:
Let the amount each nephew receives be x.
Then, each daughter receives 4x and each son receives 5x.
The total number of people receiving the money is 5+4+2 = 11.
The total amount of money is Rs 8600.
We can set up the equation: 5(5x) + 4(4x) + 2(x) = 8600
Simplifying the equation, we get 33x = 8600
Solving for x, we get x = 260
Therefore, each daughter receives 4x = 4(260) = Rs 1040.
The answer is A: Rs 400.

Action: Answer("A")

Question: A student instead of finding the value of 7/8 of a number, found the value of 7/18 of the number. If his answer differed from the actual one by 770, find the that number.
Choices:
  A: 1584
  B: 2520
  C: 1728
  D: 1656
  E: None
Response 0:
Thought:
  Let's assume the number is x.
  The student found the value of 7/18 of the number, which is (7/18)x.
  The actual value of 7/8 of the number is (7/8)x.
  The difference between the student's answer and the actual answer is 770.
  So, we can write an equation: (7/8)x - (7/18)x = 770.
  Solving for x, we get x = 2520.
  Therefore, the answer is B: 2520.

Topic: Math
Question: Calculate the maximum distance you can travel with $8.50 on a cab which charges $3.50 for the first quarter-mile and 10 cents for each additional quarter mile.
Choices:
  A: 11.75 miles
  B: 12.75 miles
  C: 17.75 miles
  D: 14.75 miles
  E: 10.75 miles
Response 0:
Thought:
  The cab charges $3.50 for the first quarter-mile and 10 cents for each additional quarter mile.
  Let's assume that the maximum distance we can travel is x miles.
  The first quarter-mile costs $3.50, which means we have $5.00 left to spend on the remaining distance.
  For each additional quarter mile, the cab charges 10 cents, which means it charges 40 cents for each mile.
  Therefore, we can write the following equation: 0.40(x - 0.25) = 5.00 - 3.50
  Solving for x, we get x = 12.75 miles.
  Therefore, the maximum distance we can travel with $8.50 is 12.75 miles.
